"From the first equation $xyz = 4$, we can rewrite it as $z = \\frac{4}{xy}$.\n\nSubstitute $z = \\frac{4}{xy}$ into the second equation $x^3 + y^3 + z^3 = 4$, we get:\n\\[x^3 + y^3 + \\left(\\frac{4}{xy}\\right)^3 = 4\\]\n\\[x^3 + y^3 + \\frac{64}{x^3y^3} = 4\\]\n\\[x^6y^3 + y^6x^3 + 64 = 4x^3y^3\\]\n\\[x^6y^3 + y^6x^3 - 4x^3y^3 + 64 = 0\\]\n\\[(x^3 - y^3)(x^3y^3 - 4) = -64\\]\n\\[(x - y)(x^2 + xy + y^2)(x^3y^3 - 4) = -64\\]\n\nNow, let's look at the third equation $xy^2 + x^2 y + xz^2 + x^2 z + yz^2 + y^2 z = 12$.\nSubstitute $z = \\frac{4}{xy}$ into the equation, we get:\n\\[xy^2 + x^2 y + x\\left(\\frac{4}{xy}\\right)^2 + x^2\\left(\\frac{4}{xy}\\right) + y\\left(\\frac{4}{xy}\\right)^2 + y^2\\left(\\frac{4}{xy}\\right) = 12\\]\n\\[xy^2 + x^2 y + \\frac{16}{x} + \\frac{4}{y} + \\frac{16}{y} + \\frac{4}{x} = 12\\]\n\\[xy^2 + x^2 y + \\frac{20}{x} + \\frac{20}{y} = 12\\]\n\\[xy^2 + x^2 y + 20\\left(\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{y}\\right) = 12\\]\n\\[xy^2 + x^2 y + 20\\left(\\frac{x+y}{xy}\\right) = 12\\]\n\\[xy^2 + x^2 y + \\frac{20(x+y)}{xy} = 12\\]\n\\[xy^3 + x^2 y^2 + 20(x+y) = 12xy\\]\n\\[xy^3 + x^2 y^2 - 12xy + 20(x+y) = 0\\]\n\\[(xy - 4)(xy^2 + 4) = 0\\]\n\\[xy = 4 \\text{ or } -4\\]\n\nSince $xy$ cannot be negative (as $xyz = 4$), we have $xy = 4$.\n\nNow, we need to find $x+y$ and $x^2 + y^2$ to calculate $xy + yz + zx$.\nFrom $xy = 4$ and $x+y = (x+y)^2 - 2xy = x^2 + y^2$, we have $x+y = 4$ and $x^2 + y^2 = 16$.\n\nTherefore, $xy + yz + zx = 4 + \\frac{4}{xy}(x+y) = 4 + \\frac{4}{4}(4) = 8$. \n\nSo, the value of $xy + yz + zx$ is $\\boxed{8}$."
"To find the area of the equiangular octagon, we can divide it into smaller shapes that are easier to work with. \n\nSince the octagon is equiangular, each interior angle measures 135 degrees. We can draw lines from each vertex to create 8 congruent isosceles triangles, each with a base of 1 and two equal sides of length $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$. \n\nNow, let's focus on one of these triangles. We can split it into two right triangles by drawing an altitude from the vertex opposite the base. This altitude will divide the base into two segments of length $\\frac{1}{2}$ each. \n\nUsing the Pythagorean theorem, we can find the height of the triangle:\n$(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2})^2 = h^2 + (\\frac{1}{2})^2$\n$\\frac{1}{2} = h^2 + \\frac{1}{4}$\n$h^2 = \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{1}{4}$\n$h^2 = 0$\n$h = 0$\n\nThis means that the altitude of the triangle is 0, which implies that the triangle is degenerate and has no area. \n\nSince all 8 triangles are degenerate, the octagon itself is also degenerate and has no area."
'To find the region of the volume enclosed by $S,$ we first need to understand the distances from point $P$ to the given planes.\n\nThe distance from a point $(x_0, y_0, z_0)$ to a plane $Ax + By + Cz + D = 0$ is given by the formula:\n\\[d = \\frac{|Ax_0 + By_0 + Cz_0 + D|}{\\sqrt{A^2 + B^2 + C^2}}.\\]\n\nGiven the planes $x - z = 0,$ $x - 2y + z = 0,$ and $x + y + z = 0,$ we can rewrite them in the form $Ax + By + Cz + D = 0$ as follows:\n1. $x - z = 0$ can be written as $x - 0y - z + 0 = 0,$ so $A = 1,$ $B = 0,$ $C = -1,$ and $D = 0.$\n2. $x - 2y + z = 0$ can be written as $x - 2y + z + 0 = 0,$ so $A = 1,$ $B = -2,$ $C = 1,$ and $D = 0.$\n3. $x + y + z = 0$ can be written as $x + y + z + 0 = 0,$ so $A = 1,$ $B = 1,$ $C = 1,$ and $D = 0.$\n\nNow, we can calculate the distances $d_1,$ $d_2,$ and $d_3$ from point $P(x, y, z)$ to the planes using the formula above:\n1. $d_1 = \\frac{|x - z|}{\\sqrt{1^2 + 0^2 + (-1)^2}} = \\frac{|x - z|}{\\sqrt{2}}$\n2. $d_2 = \\frac{|x - 2y + z|}{\\sqrt{1^2 + (-2)^2 + 1^2}} = \\frac{|x - 2y + z|}{\\sqrt{6}}$\n3. $d_3 = \\frac{|x + y + z|}{\\sqrt{1^2 + 1^2 + 1^2}} = \\frac{|x + y + z|}{\\sqrt{3}}$\n\nGiven that $d_1^2 + d_2^2 + d_3^2 = 36,$ we have:\n\\[\\left(\\frac{|x - z|}{\\sqrt{2}}\\right)^2 + \\left(\\frac{|x - 2y + z|}{\\sqrt{6}}\\right)^2 + \\left(\\frac{|x + y + z|}{\\sqrt{3}}\\right)^2 = 36.\\]\n\nSolving this equation will give us the region of the volume enclosed by $S.$ This involves considering different cases based on the signs of $x - z,$ $x - 2y + z,$ and $x + y + z.$ By analyzing these cases and solving the equation, we can determine the specific region of the volume enclosed by $S.$'
"From the given recursive formula $f(n + 1) = (-1)^{n + 1} n - 2f(n)$ for $n \\ge 1$ and the initial condition $f(1) = f(1986)$, we can find a pattern in the values of $f(n)$.\n\nLet's calculate the first few values of $f(n)$:\n$f(2) = (-1)^2 \\cdot 1 - 2f(1) = -1 - 2f(1)$\n$f(3) = (-1)^3 \\cdot 2 - 2f(2) = -2 - 2(-1 - 2f(1)) = 4f(1) - 4$\n$f(4) = (-1)^4 \\cdot 3 - 2f(3) = 3 - 2(4f(1) - 4) = -8f(1) + 11$\n$f(5) = (-1)^5 \\cdot 4 - 2f(4) = -4 - 2(-8f(1) + 11) = 16f(1) - 29$\n\nWe can see that the coefficients of $f(1)$ in $f(2), f(3), f(4), f(5)$ are $-2, 4, -8, 16$ respectively. This forms a geometric sequence with first term $-2$ and common ratio $-2$. Therefore, the general formula for $f(n)$ in terms of $f(1)$ is $f(n) = -2 \\cdot (-2)^{n-2}f(1) + (2^{n-1} - 1)$.\n\nSince $f(1) = f(1986)$, we have $f(1986) = -2 \\cdot (-2)^{1986-2}f(1) + (2^{1986-1} - 1)$. Simplifying this equation gives $f(1986) = -2^{1985}f(1) + 2^{1985} - 1$.\n\nNow, we need to find the sum $f(1) + f(2) + f(3) + \\dots + f(1985)$. This sum can be written as:\n\\[f(1) + f(2) + f(3) + \\dots + f(1985) = -2f(1) + (2^0 - 1) - 2^2f(1) + (2^1 - 1) - 2^3f(1) + (2^2 - 1) + \\dots - 2^{1984}f(1) + (2^{1983} - 1)\\]\n\\[= f(1986) - 2^{1985}f(1) + 2^{1985} - 1\\]\n\\[= -2^{1985}f(1) + 2^{1985} - 1 - 2^{1985}f(1) + 2^{1985} - 1\\]\n\\[= -2 \\cdot 2^{1985}f(1) + 2 \\cdot 2^{1985} - 2\\]\n\\[= -2^{1986}f(1) + 2^{1986} - 2\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum $f(1) + f(2) + f(3) + \\dots + f(1985)$ is equal to $-2^{1986}f(1) + 2^{1986} - 2$."

Since $a$ is negative and $b$ is positive, we want $a$ to be as close to $-6$ and $b$ to be as close to $3$ to maximize the product.\n\nLet's consider the expression $\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right)$:\n\n$\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right) = a\\left(\\frac{1}{b}\\right) + \\frac{1}{b}\\left(\\frac{1}{b}\\right) - a\\left(\\frac{1}{b}\\right) - a^2$\n\nNow, substitute the values that maximize the expression:\n\n$a = -6$ and $b = 3$\n\nPlugging in these values, we get:\n\n$\\displaystyle\\left(-6+\\frac{1}{3}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{3}-(-6)\\right) = \\left(-6+\\frac{1}{3}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{3}+6\\right) = \\left(-\\frac{17}{3}\\right)\\left(\\frac{19}{3}\\right) = -\\frac{323}{9}$\n\nTherefore, the greatest possible value of $\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right)$ is $\\boxed{-\\frac{323}{9}}$."

'To find the value of $x_{531}+x_{753}+x_{975}$, we first need to find the pattern in the given sequence.\n\nGiven that $x_{n}=x_{n-1}-x_{n-2}+x_{n-3}-x_{n-4}$ for $n\\geq5$, we can start by finding the values of $x_5, x_6, x_7, x_8$ and so on.\n\n\\begin{align*}\nx_{5} &= x_{4}-x_{3}+x_{2}-x_{1} \\\\\n&= 523 - 420 + 375 - 211 \\\\\n&= 267\n\\end{align*}\n\n\\begin{align*}\nx_{6} &= x_{5}-x_{4}+x_{3}-x_{2} \\\\\n&= 267 - 523 + 420 - 375 \\\\\n&= -211\n\\end{align*}\n\n\\begin{align*}\nx_{7} &= x_{6}-x_{5}+x_{4}-x_{3} \\\\\n&= -211 - 267 + 523 - 420 \\\\\n&= -375\n\\end{align*}\n\n\\begin{align*}\nx_{8} &= x_{7}-x_{6}+x_{5}-x_{4} \\\\\n&= -375 + 211 - 267 + 523 \\\\\n&= 92\n\\end{align*}\n\nContinuing this pattern, we can find the values of $x_{9}, x_{10}, x_{11}, ...$ until we reach $x_{531}, x_{753},$ and $x_{975}$.\n\nSince the pattern repeats every 4 terms, we can simplify the problem by finding the remainder when dividing the given indices by 4.\n\nFor $531$, the remainder when divided by $4$ is $3$, so $x_{531} = x_{3} = 420$.\n\nFor $753$, the remainder when divided by $4$ is $1$, so $x_{753} = x_{1} = 211$.\n\nFor $975$, the remainder when divided by $4$ is $3$, so $x_{975} = x_{3} = 420$.\n\nTherefore, $x_{531}+x_{753}+x_{975} = 420 + 211 + 420 = \\boxed{1051}$.'
"To find the distinct possible values for $B$, we need to consider the possible values for the tens digit in the square of a positive integer.\n\nSince the two-digit number $``B6''$ is the square of a positive integer, it can be written as $10B + 6$. This number must be a perfect square, so we can express it as $(a)^2$ for some positive integer $a$.\n\nTherefore, we have:\n$(10B + 6) = a^2$\n\nExpanding the left side, we get:\n$10B + 6 = a^2$\n\nRearranging the equation, we have:\n$10B = a^2 - 6$\n\nSince $10B$ is a multiple of 10, $a^2 - 6$ must also be a multiple of 10. This means that $a^2$ must end in 6, which limits the possible values for $a$.\n\nThe perfect squares that end in 6 are 16, 36, 56, and 76. Therefore, the possible values for $a$ are 4, 6, 8, and 9.\n\nSubstitute these values back into the equation $10B = a^2 - 6$ to find the corresponding values for $B$:\nFor $a = 4$: $10B = 16 - 6 \\Rightarrow 10B = 10 \\Rightarrow B = 1$\nFor $a = 6$: $10B = 36 - 6 \\Rightarrow 10B = 30 \\Rightarrow B = 3$\nFor $a = 8$: $10B = 64 - 6 \\Rightarrow 10B = 58$ (not a valid value for $B$)\nFor $a = 9$: $10B = 81 - 6 \\Rightarrow 10B = 75$ (not a valid value for $B$)\n\nTherefore, the distinct possible values for $B$ are 1 and 3. So, there are 2 distinct possible values for $B$."

Since the total area of the shaded region is $\\frac{5}{12}$ of the area of the larger circle, we have:\n\n$\\pi r_2^2 - \\pi r_1^2 = \\frac{5}{12} \\pi r_2^2$\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n$\\pi (r_2^2 - r_1^2) = \\frac{5}{12} \\pi r_2^2$\n\n$r_2^2 - r_1^2 = \\frac{5}{12} r_2^2$\n\n$r_2^2 - r_1^2 = \\frac{5}{12} r_2^2$\n\n$12r_2^2 - 12r_1^2 = 5r_2^2$\n\n$7r_2^2 = 12r_1^2$\n\n$r_2 = \\frac{2}{\\sqrt{7}} r_1$\n\nSince the radii are $1$ and $2$, we have $r_1 = 1$ and $r_2 = 2\\sqrt{7}$. \n\nNow, let's consider the triangle $\\triangle ADC$. "To find the area of the equiangular octagon with alternating side lengths of $1$ and $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$, we can divide the octagon into smaller shapes that are easier to work with. \n\nFirst, let's consider the regular octagon with side length $1$. The area of a regular octagon can be calculated using the formula $A = 2(1 + \\sqrt{2})s^2$, where $s$ is the side length. Substituting $s = 1$ into the formula, we get:\n\n$A = 2(1 + \\sqrt{2})(1)^2 = 2(1 + \\sqrt{2}) = 2 + 2\\sqrt{2}$\n\nSo, the area of the regular octagon with side length $1$ is $2 + 2\\sqrt{2}$.\n\nNext, let's consider the regular octagon with side length $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$. The area of this octagon can be calculated using the same formula:\n\n$A = 2(1 + \\sqrt{2})(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2})^2 = 2(1 + \\sqrt{2})\\frac{1}{2} = (1 + \\sqrt{2})$\n\nSo, the area of the regular octagon with side length $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$ is $1 + \\sqrt{2}$.\n\nNow, the equiangular octagon with alternating side lengths of $1$ and $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$ can be divided into smaller regular octagons with side lengths $1$ and $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$. The total area of the equiangular octagon is the sum of the areas of these regular octagons:\n\n$2(2 + 2\\sqrt{2}) + 6(1 + \\sqrt{2}) = 4 + 4\\sqrt{2} + 6 + 6\\sqrt{2} = 10 + 10\\sqrt{2}$\n\nTherefore, the area of the equiangular octagon with alternating side lengths of $1$ and $\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}$ is $10 + 10\\sqrt{2}$."
'Given that $|z| = 1,$ we can write $z = \\cos \\theta + i \\sin \\theta$ for some real number $\\theta.$  Then\n\\[|1 + z| = |1 + \\cos \\theta + i \\sin \\theta| = \\sqrt{(1 + \\cos \\theta)^2 + \\sin^2 \\theta} = \\sqrt{2 + 2 \\cos \\theta}.\\]Also,\n\\begin{align*}\n1 - z + z^2 &= 1 - (\\cos \\theta + i \\sin \\theta) + (\\cos \\theta + i \\sin \\theta)^2 \\\\\n&= 1 - \\cos \\theta - i \\sin \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta - \\sin^2 \\theta + 2i \\cos \\theta \\sin \\theta \\\\\n&= 1 - \\cos \\theta - i \\sin \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta - \\sin^2 \\theta + 2i \\cos \\theta \\sin \\theta \\\\\n&= 1 - \\cos \\theta - i \\sin \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta - (1 - \\cos^2 \\theta) + 2i \\cos \\theta \\sin \\theta \\\\\n&= 2 \\cos^2 \\theta - \\cos \\theta + 2i \\cos \\theta \\sin \\theta.\n\\end{align*}Then\n\\begin{align*}\n|1 - z + z^2| &= |2 \\cos^2 \\theta - \\cos \\theta + 2i \\cos \\theta \\sin \\theta| \\\\\n&= \\sqrt{(2 \\cos^2 \\theta - \\cos \\theta)^2 + (2 \\cos \\theta \\sin \\theta)^2} \\\\\n&= \\sqrt{4 \\cos^4 \\theta - 4 \\cos^3 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta + 4 \\cos^2 \\theta \\sin^2 \\theta} \\\\\n&= \\sqrt{4 \\cos^4 \\theta - 4 \\cos^3 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta + 4 \\cos^2 \\theta (1 - \\cos^2 \\theta)} \\\\\n&= \\sqrt{4 \\cos^4 \\theta - 4 \\cos^3 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta + 4 \\cos^2 \\theta - 4 \\cos^4 \\theta} \\\\\n&= \\sqrt{4 - 4 \\cos^3 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta}.\n\\end{align*}Therefore,\n\\[|1 + z| + |1 - z + z^2| = \\sqrt{2 + 2 \\cos \\theta} + \\sqrt{4 - 4 \\cos^3 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta}.\\]By Cauchy-Schwarz,\n\\[(1 + 1)(2 + 1) \\ge (\\sqrt{2} + \\sqrt{2 \\cos \\theta})(\\sqrt{1} + \\sqrt{1 + \\cos^2 \\theta}),\\]so\n\\[3 \\ge \\sqrt{2 + 2 \\cos \\theta} + \\sqrt{4 - 4 \\cos^3 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta}.\\]Equality occurs when $\\cos \\theta = 1,$ so the maximum value is $\\boxed{3}.$'

"Given that $-6\\leq a \\leq -2$ and $3 \\leq b \\leq 5$, we need to find the greatest possible value of $\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right)$.\n\nLet's first simplify the expression:\n$\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right) = a\\left(\\frac{1}{b}\\right) + \\frac{1}{b}\\left(\\frac{1}{b}\\right) - a\\left(\\frac{1}{b}\\right) - a^{2} = \\frac{a}{b} + \\frac{1}{b^{2}} - \\frac{a}{b} - a^{2} = \\frac{1}{b^{2}} - a^{2}$\n\nTo maximize $\\frac{1}{b^{2}} - a^{2}$, we need to minimize $a^{2}$ and maximize $\\frac{1}{b^{2}}$.\n\nSince $-6\\leq a \\leq -2$, to minimize $a^{2}$, we choose $a=-2$.\nSince $3 \\leq b \\leq 5$, to maximize $\\frac{1}{b^{2}}$, we choose $b=3$.\n\nTherefore, the greatest possible value of $\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right)$ is:\n$\\frac{1}{3^{2}} - (-2)^{2} = \\frac{1}{9} - 4 = -\\frac{35}{9}$\n\nSo, the greatest possible value of $\\displaystyle\\left(a+\\frac{1}{b}\\right)\\left(\\frac{1}{b}-a\\right)$ is $\\boxed{-\\frac{35}{9}}$."
"To determine the values of $x$ for which the inequality $\\frac{1}{x - 5} > 0$ is true, we need to find when the fraction is positive. \n\nFor a fraction to be positive, the numerator and denominator must have the same sign. Since the numerator is always positive (1), the denominator $(x - 5)$ must also be positive for the fraction to be positive.\n\nTherefore, we have $x - 5 > 0$, which simplifies to $x > 5$. This means that the values of $x$ for which the inequality $\\frac{1}{x - 5} > 0$ is true are $x > 5$.\n\nNow, let's go back to the original problem. We are given that $ab^2 = 5$. We want to find the minimum value of $a^4 + b^8$.\n\nUsing the given equation, we can express $a$ in terms of $b$ as $a = \\frac{5}{b^2}$. Substituting this into the expression $a^4 + b^8$, we get:\n\n$a^4 + b^8 = \\left(\\frac{5}{b^2}\\right)^4 + b^8 = \\frac{625}{b^8} + b^8$\n\nNow, we need to find the minimum value of this expression. To do this, we can use the AM-GM inequality, which states that for any non-negative real numbers $x$ and $y$, $\\frac{x + y}{2} \\geq \\sqrt{xy}$.\n\nApplying AM-GM to $\\frac{625}{b^8}$ and $b^8$, we have:\n\n$\\frac{\\frac{625}{b^8} + b^8}{2} \\geq \\sqrt{\\frac{625}{b^8} \\cdot b^8}$\n\nSimplifying the right side gives:\n\n$\\frac{\\frac{625}{b^8} + b^8}{2} \\geq \\sqrt{625} = 25$\n\nTherefore, $\\frac{625}{b^8} + b^8 \\geq 2 \\cdot 25 = 50$.\n\nThe minimum value of $a^4 + b^8$ is $50$, and it occurs when $a = 5$ and $b = 1$."
'To solve the inequality $-4<x^{4}+4x^{2}<21$, we can treat it as a quadratic inequality by letting $y=x^{2}$. This gives us $-4<y^{2}+4y<21$. \n\nNow, we can solve this quadratic inequality by finding the roots of the quadratic equation $y^{2}+4y-4=0$. The roots are $y=-2\\pm2\\sqrt{2}$. \n\nTherefore, the solutions for $y$ are $-2-2\\sqrt{2}<y<-2+2\\sqrt{2}$. \n\nSince $y=x^{2}$, we have $-2-2\\sqrt{2}<x^{2}<-2+2\\sqrt{2}$. \n\nTaking the square root of each part of the inequality, we get $\\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}}<x<\\sqrt{-2+2\\sqrt{2}}$. \n\nHowever, since we are looking for real values of $x$, we need to consider the negative square root as well. Therefore, the final solution is $-\\sqrt{-2+2\\sqrt{2}}<x<-\\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}} \\cup \\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}}<x<\\sqrt{-2+2\\sqrt{2}}$.\n\nCalculating the values of $x_{531}$, $x_{753}$, and $x_{975}$, we get:\n$x_{531} = -\\sqrt{-2+2\\sqrt{2}}$\n$x_{753} = -\\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}}$\n$x_{975} = \\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}}$\n\nTherefore, $x_{531}+x_{753}+x_{975} = -\\sqrt{-2+2\\sqrt{2}} - \\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}} + \\sqrt{-2-2\\sqrt{2}}$.'

'To find out how much Susan and Pam pay for their tickets, we first need to calculate the discounted price of one ticket for each of them.\n\nFor Susan:\nDiscounted price of one ticket = $20 - 25\\% \\times 20 = 20 - 0.25 \\times 20 = 20 - 5 = $15\nSusan buys 4 tickets, so she pays $15 \\times 4 = $60 in total.\n\nFor Pam:\nDiscounted price of one ticket = $20 - 30\\% \\times 20 = 20 - 0.30 \\times 20 = 20 - 6 = $14\nPam buys 5 tickets, so she pays $14 \\times 5 = $70 in total.\n\nThe difference in the amount paid by Pam and Susan is $70 - $60 = $10. \n\nTherefore, Pam pays $10 more than Susan for the tickets.'
'To find the length of the shortest path the gecko can take to reach the fly, we can visualize the room as a rectangular prism. The gecko is currently on a side wall that is 10 feet wide and 8 feet tall, one foot from the ceiling and one foot from the back wall. The fly is on the opposite side wall that is also 10 feet wide and 8 feet tall, one foot from the floor and one foot from the front wall.\n\nSince the gecko can only walk across the ceiling and walls, the shortest path for the gecko to reach the fly is to move along the ceiling to the front wall, then move across the front wall to the floor, and finally move along the floor to the fly. This path forms a right triangle with legs of length 10 feet and 7 feet (8 feet - 1 foot - 1 foot).\n\nUsing the Pythagorean theorem, the length of the shortest path the gecko can take to reach the fly is:\n$\\sqrt{10^2 + 7^2} = \\sqrt{100 + 49} = \\sqrt{149}$ feet.\n\nTherefore, the length of the shortest path the gecko can take to reach the fly is $\\boxed{\\sqrt{149}}$ feet.\n\n---\n\nTo find the quotient when the polynomial $x^6 - 3$ is divided by $x + 1$, we can use polynomial long division.\n\nDividing $x^6 - 3$ by $x + 1$:\n```\n          x^5 - x^4 + x^3 - x^2 + x - 1\n    _________________________________\nx + 1 | x^6 + 0x^5 + 0x^4 + 0x^3 + 0x^2 + 0x - 3\n          - (x^6 + x^5)\n          ______________\n                    - x^5 + 0x^4\n                    - (- x^5 - x^4)\n                    ______________\n                               x^4 + 0x^3\n                               - (x^4 + x^3)\n                               ______________\n                                         - x^3 + 0x^2\n                                         - (- x^3 - x^2)\n                                         ______________\n                                                   x^2 + 0x\n                                                   - (x^2 + x)\n                                                   ______________\n                                                             - x - 3\n                                                             - (- x - 1)\n                                                             ______________\n                                                                       -2\n```\n\nTherefore, the quotient when $x^6 - 3$ is divided by $x + 1$ is $\\boxed{x^5 - x^4 + x^3 - x^2 + x - 1}$ with a remainder of -2.'
"Given $f(x) = \\frac{\\sqrt{x-1}}{x-2}$, in order for $f(x)$ to have a real number value, the expression under the square root, $x-1$, must be greater than or equal to 0. This means $x \\geq 1$. Additionally, the denominator $x-2$ cannot be equal to 0, so $x \\neq 2$.\n\nSince we are looking for the smallest possible integer value for $x$, we start with $x = 1$. However, $x = 1$ does not satisfy the condition $x \\neq 2$. Therefore, we move on to the next smallest integer, which is $x = 3$. \n\nFor $x = 3$, $f(3) = \\frac{\\sqrt{3-1}}{3-2} = \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{1} = \\sqrt{2}$, which is a real number value. This occurs when $z$ is diametrically opposite to $1$ on the unit circle. 'The irreducible polynomials in the factorization of $x^8 + 3x^4 - 4$ are $x^4 + 4$ and $x^4 - 1$. \n\nTo find the sum of the values of each irreducible polynomial $p_i(x)$ evaluated at $x = 1$, we simply substitute $x = 1$ into each polynomial and sum the results.\n\nFor $p_1(x) = x^4 + 4$, we have:\n$p_1(1) = 1^4 + 4 = 1 + 4 = 5$\n\nFor $p_2(x) = x^4 - 1$, we have:\n$p_2(1) = 1^4 - 1 = 1 - 1 = 0$\n\nTherefore, the sum of the values of each irreducible polynomial $p_i(x)$ evaluated at $x = 1$ is $5 + 0 = 5$.'

"Given that $ab^2 = 5$, we want to find the minimum value of $a^4 + b^8$.\n\nLet's first express $b$ in terms of $a$ using the given constraint $ab^2 = 5$:\n\\[b = \\frac{5}{a^2}\\]\n\nNow, substitute this expression for $b$ into the expression we want to minimize:\n\\[a^4 + \\left(\\frac{5}{a^2}\\right)^8 = a^4 + \\frac{390625}{a^{16}}\\]\n\nTo find the minimum value of this expression, we can use calculus. Let $f(a) = a^4 + \\frac{390625}{a^{16}}$. To find the minimum, we need to find where the derivative of $f(a)$ is equal to zero:\n\\[f'(a) = 4a^3 - 6240a^{-17}\\]\n\nSetting $f'(a) = 0$:\n\\[4a^3 - 6240a^{-17} = 0\\]\n\\[4a^{20} - 6240 = 0\\]\n\\[a^{20} = 1560\\]\n\\[a = \\sqrt[20]{1560}\\]\n\nNow, substitute this value of $a$ back into the expression $a^4 + \\frac{390625}{a^{16}}$ to find the minimum value:\n\\[a^4 + \\frac{390625}{a^{16}} = \\left(\\sqrt[20]{1560}\\right)^4 + \\frac{390625}{\\left(\\sqrt[20]{1560}\\right)^{16}}\\]\n\nCalculating this value will give you the minimum value of $a^4 + b^8$ given the constraint $ab^2 = 5$."
'To find the real values of $x$ that satisfy the inequality $-4<x^{4}+4x^{2}<21$, we can follow the steps provided in the hint.\n\n1. The inequality is $-4<x^{4}+4x^{2}<21$.\n2. We need to find the real values of $x$ that satisfy the inequality.\n3. The inequality can be simplified to $-4<x^{2}(x^{2}+4)<21$.\n4. We can further simplify the inequality to $-4<x^{2}<21/(x^{2}+4)$.\n5. To find the real values of $x$, we need to consider the cases when $x^{2}$ is positive and negative.\n\nCase 1: $x^{2}$ is positive\nIn this case, the inequality $-4<x^{2}<21/(x^{2}+4)$ holds true.\nSolving $-4<x^{2}$ gives $x^{2}>-4$, which is always true for real numbers.\nSolving $x^{2}<21/(x^{2}+4)$ gives $x^{4}+4x^{2}<21$, which is the original inequality.\n\nCase 2: $x^{2}$ is negative\nIn this case, the inequality $-4<x^{2}<21/(x^{2}+4)$ also holds true.\nSolving $-4<x^{2}$ gives $x^{2}>-4$, which is not possible for negative $x^{2}$.\nSolving $x^{2}<21/(x^{2}+4)$ gives $x^{4}+4x^{2}<21$, which is the original inequality.\n\nTherefore, the real values of $x$ that satisfy the inequality $-4<x^{4}+4x^{2}<21$ are all real numbers.'

By Vieta's formulas, we have:\n\\[p + q + r = -a\\]\n\\[pq + pr + qr = a\\]\n\\[pqr = -1\\]\n\nWe are given the expression involving trigonometric functions of arcsines:\n\\[\\sin (\\arcsin 0.4 + \\arcsin 0.5) \\cdot \\sin (\\arcsin 0.5 - \\arcsin 0.4)\\]\n\nUsing the angle addition formula for sine, we have:\n\\[\\sin (\\arcsin x + \\arcsin y) = x\\sqrt{1-y^2} + y\\sqrt{1-x^2}\\]\n\nApplying this formula to the given expression, we get:\n\\[\\sin (\\arcsin 0.4 + \\arcsin 0.5) = 0.4\\sqrt{1-0.5^2} + 0.5\\sqrt{1-0.4^2} = 0.4\\sqrt{0.75} + 0.5\\sqrt{0.84}\\]\n\nSimilarly, we can find:\n\\[\\sin (\\arcsin 0.5 - \\arcsin 0.4) = 0.5\\sqrt{1-0.4^2} - 0.4\\sqrt{1-0.5^2} = 0.5\\sqrt{0.84} - 0.4\\sqrt{0.75}\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of the expression is:\n\\[0.4\\sqrt{0.75} + 0.5\\sqrt{0.84} \\cdot (0.5\\sqrt{0.84} - 0.4\\sqrt{0.75})\\]\n\\[= 0.4\\sqrt{0.75} + 0.5\\sqrt{0.84} \\cdot 0.5\\sqrt{0.84} - 0.5\\sqrt{0.84} \\cdot 0.4\\sqrt{0.75}\\]\n\\[= 0.4\\sqrt{0.75} + 0.42 - 0.42\\]\n\\[= 0.4\\sqrt{0.75}\\]\n\nTo find the smallest possible value of $a$, we need to minimize $a$. From Vieta's formulas, we know that $a = -(p+q+r)$. Since $p$, $q$, and $r$ are the roots of the polynomial $x^3 + ax^2 + ax + 1 = 0$, we can rewrite the polynomial as:\n\\[(x-p)(x-q)(x-r) = 0\\]\n\\[x^3 - (p+q+r)x^2 + (pq + pr + qr)x - pqr = 0\\]\n\\[x^3 + ax^2 + ax + 1 = 0\\]\n\nComparing coefficients, we get:\n\\[p+q+r = -a\\]\n\\[pq + pr + qr = a\\]\n\\[pqr = -1\\]\n\nSince $pqr = -1$, we have $p = \\frac{-1}{qr}$. "To find the eighth term of the geometric sequence $\\frac{125}{9}, \\frac{25}{3}, 5, 3, \\ldots$, we first need to determine the common ratio. \n\nThe common ratio, denoted by $r$, can be found by dividing any term by the previous term. Let's take the second and first terms to find $r$:\n$r = \\frac{\\frac{25}{3}}{\\frac{125}{9}} = \\frac{25}{3} \\times \\frac{9}{125} = \\frac{225}{375} = \\frac{3}{5}$\n\nNow that we have the common ratio, we can find the eighth term of the sequence:\n$a_n = a_1 \\times r^{(n-1)}$\n$a_8 = \\frac{125}{9} \\times \\left(\\frac{3}{5}\\right)^7 = \\frac{125}{9} \\times \\frac{2187}{78125} = \\frac{125 \\times 2187}{9 \\times 78125} = \\frac{27375}{78125}$\n\nTherefore, the eighth term of the sequence is $\\frac{27375}{78125}$.\n\nMoving on to the second part of the question, we are given that the altitude to the hypotenuse of an isosceles right triangle has length $4\\sqrt{2}$. \n\nIn an isosceles right triangle, the altitude to the hypotenuse divides the triangle into two smaller congruent right triangles. Since the altitude divides the hypotenuse into two segments of equal length, each segment has length $4\\sqrt{2}$. \n\nUsing the Pythagorean theorem, we can find the length of the hypotenuse:\n$h^2 = (4\\sqrt{2})^2 + (4\\sqrt{2})^2$\n$h^2 = 32 + 32$\n$h^2 = 64$\n$h = \\sqrt{64}$\n$h = 8$\n\nThe hypotenuse of the isosceles right triangle has a length of 8. \n\nTo find the area of the isosceles right triangle, we can use the formula for the area of a triangle:\n$A = \\frac{1}{2} \\times \\text{base} \\times \\text{height}$\n$A = \\frac{1}{2} \\times 8 \\times 8$\n$A = \\frac{1}{2} \\times 64$\n$A = 32$\n\nTherefore, the area of the isosceles right triangle is 32 square units."

'To ensure that all the roots of the cubic equation $x^3 + ax^2 + ax + 1 = 0$ are real, we need to make sure that the discriminant of the cubic equation is non-negative.\n\nThe discriminant of a cubic equation $ax^3 + bx^2 + cx + d = 0$ is given by $\\Delta = 18abcd - 4b^3d + b^2c^2 - 4ac^3 - 27a^2d^2$.\n\nIn this case, the coefficients of the cubic equation are $a = 1$, $b = a$, $c = a$, and $d = 1$. Substituting these values into the formula for the discriminant, we get:\n\n$\\Delta = 18(1)(1)(1)(1) - 4a^3(1) + a^2(a)^2 - 4(1)(a)^3 - 27(1)^2(1)^2$\n$\\Delta = 18 - 4a^3 + a^3 - 4a^3 - 27$\n$\\Delta = -7a^3 - 9$\n\nFor the roots of the cubic equation to be real, the discriminant $\\Delta$ must be non-negative. Therefore, we have:\n\n$-7a^3 - 9 \\geq 0$\n$-7a^3 \\geq 9$\n$a^3 \\leq -\\frac{9}{7}$\n\nSince $a^3$ must be negative for $a$ to be real, the smallest possible value of $a$ that satisfies this condition is $a = -\\sqrt[3]{\\frac{9}{7}}$.'

'The given equation is in polar form, where $r$ represents the distance from the origin and $\\theta$ represents the angle from the positive x-axis.\n\nTo determine the curve defined by the equation $r^2 \\cos 2 \\theta = 4$, we can rewrite it in terms of $x$ and $y$ using the relationships $x = r \\cos \\theta$ and $y = r \\sin \\theta$.\n\nSubstitute $r^2 = x^2 + y^2$ and $\\cos 2\\theta = \\cos^2 \\theta - \\sin^2 \\theta = 2\\cos^2 \\theta - 1$ into the equation:\n\\[r^2 \\cos 2 \\theta = 4\\]\n\\[(x^2 + y^2)(2\\cos^2 \\theta - 1) = 4\\]\n\\[2x^2\\cos^2 \\theta + 2y^2\\cos^2 \\theta - x^2 - y^2 = 4\\]\n\\[2x^2\\left(\\frac{x^2}{x^2 + y^2}\\right) + 2y^2\\left(\\frac{y^2}{x^2 + y^2}\\right) - x^2 - y^2 = 4\\]\n\\[2x^4 + 2y^4 - x^2(x^2 + y^2) - y^2(x^2 + y^2) = 4(x^2 + y^2)\\]\n\\[2x^4 + 2y^4 - x^4 - x^2y^2 - y^4 - x^2y^2 = 4(x^2 + y^2)\\]\n\\[x^4 - 2x^2y^2 + y^4 = 4(x^2 + y^2)\\]\n\nThis equation represents an ellipse, as it is in the standard form of the equation of an ellipse:\n\\[\\frac{x^2}{a^2} + \\frac{y^2}{b^2} = 1\\]\nwhere $a$ and $b$ are the semi-major and semi-minor axes of the ellipse, respectively.\n\nTherefore, the curve defined by the equation $r^2 \\cos 2 \\theta = 4$ is an ellipse. The answer is (D) Ellipse.\n\nFor the second question, to find the value of $x$ that makes $2^3 \\cdot 3^x = 72$ true, we can rewrite $72$ as $2^3 \\cdot 3^2$. Therefore, we have:\n\\[2^3 \\cdot 3^x = 2^3 \\cdot 3^2\\]\n\\[3^x = 3^2\\]\n\\[x = 2\\]\n\nSo, the value of $x$ that makes $2^3 \\cdot 3^x = 72$ true is $x = 2$.'
'To find $w$, we first need to find the vector $\\overrightarrow{cz}$ and then rotate it by $\\frac{\\pi}{4}$ counter-clockwise.\n\nGiven that $z = 2 + \\sqrt{2} - (3 + 3 \\sqrt{2})i$ and $c = 2 - 3i$, we can find $\\overrightarrow{cz}$ as follows:\n\\begin{align*}\n\\overrightarrow{cz} &= \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ -3 \\end{pmatrix} - \\begin{pmatrix} 2 + \\sqrt{2} \\\\ 3 + 3\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix} \\\\\n&= \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ -3 \\end{pmatrix} - \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 3 \\end{pmatrix} - \\begin{pmatrix} \\sqrt{2} \\\\ 3\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix} \\\\\n&= \\begin{pmatrix} 0 \\\\ -6 \\end{pmatrix} - \\begin{pmatrix} \\sqrt{2} \\\\ 3\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix} \\\\\n&= \\begin{pmatrix} -\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -9\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix}\n\\end{align*}\n\nNow, to rotate $\\overrightarrow{cz}$ by $\\frac{\\pi}{4}$ counter-clockwise, we can use the rotation matrix:\n\\[\n\\begin{pmatrix} \\cos(\\frac{\\pi}{4}) & -\\sin(\\frac{\\pi}{4}) \\\\ \\sin(\\frac{\\pi}{4}) & \\cos(\\frac{\\pi}{4}) \\end{pmatrix} = \\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} & -\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\\\ \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} & \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\end{pmatrix}\n\\]\n\nMultiplying this matrix by $\\overrightarrow{cz}$, we get:\n\\[\n\\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} & -\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\\\ \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} & \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\end{pmatrix} \\begin{pmatrix} -\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -9\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix} = \\begin{pmatrix} 6\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -6\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the vector $\\overrightarrow{cw}$ is $\\begin{pmatrix} 6\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -6\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix}$, which means $w = c + \\begin{pmatrix} 6\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -6\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix} = \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ -3 \\end{pmatrix} + \\begin{pmatrix} 6\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -6\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix} = \\begin{pmatrix} 2 + 6\\sqrt{2} \\\\ -3 - 6\\sqrt{2} \\end{pmatrix}$.\n\nTherefore, $w = 2 + 6\\sqrt{2} - (3 + 6\\sqrt{2})i = \\boxed{-1 - 3\\sqrt{2} - 6i}$.'

Since $2$ is the largest value, the smallest positive real number $C$ is $\\boxed{2}.$'
'To find the $y$-intercepts of the parabola $x = y^2 - 4y - 1$, we need to set $x$ to zero and solve for $y$.\n\nGiven equation: $x = y^2 - 4y - 1$\n\nSetting $x$ to zero: $0 = y^2 - 4y - 1$\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in the form $ay^2 + by + c = 0$, where $a = 1$, $b = -4$, and $c = -1$. \n\nTo find the $y$-intercepts, we need to find the values of $y$ when $x = 0$. We can solve the quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\nThe quadratic formula is given by: $y = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}$\n\nPlugging in the values $a = 1$, $b = -4$, and $c = -1$ into the formula, we get:\n\n$y = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{(-4)^2 - 4(1)(-1)}}{2(1)}$\n\n$y = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 4}}{2}$\n\n$y = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{20}}{2}$\n\n$y = \\frac{4 \\pm 2\\sqrt{5}}{2}$\n\n$y = 2 \\pm \\sqrt{5}$\n\nTherefore, the parabola $x = y^2 - 4y - 1$ has two $y$-intercepts at $y = 2 + \\sqrt{5}$ and $y = 2 - \\sqrt{5}$.'
"To solve for $x$ in the equation $\\frac{x}{2} + \\frac{x}{3} = 5$, we first need to find a common denominator for $\\frac{1}{2}$ and $\\frac{1}{3}$. The common denominator is 6. \n\nRewriting the equation with the common denominator, we get $\\frac{3x}{6} + \\frac{2x}{6} = 5$. Combining the fractions, we have $\\frac{5x}{6} = 5$. \n\nTo isolate $x$, we multiply both sides of the equation by the reciprocal of $\\frac{5}{6}$, which is $\\frac{6}{5}$. This gives us $x = 5 \\times \\frac{6}{5} = 6$.\n\nTherefore, the solution to the equation $\\frac{x}{2} + \\frac{x}{3} = 5$ is $x = 6$.\n\nNow, let's move on to the second part of the question. \n\nGiven that the volume of a cube is $1$ cubic foot, we know that each side of the cube is $\\sqrt[3]{1} = 1$ foot long. \n\nTo find the total surface area of the cube, we need to calculate the area of each face and then sum them up. Since a cube has 6 faces, each face is a square with side length 1 foot. \n\nThe area of each face is $1 \\text{ foot} \\times 1 \\text{ foot} = 1 \\text{ square foot}$. \n\nTo convert the area from square feet to square inches, we know that 1 square foot is equal to 144 square inches (since 1 foot = 12 inches, and $1 \\text{ foot} \\times 1 \\text{ foot} = 12 \\text{ inches} \\times 12 \\text{ inches} = 144 \\text{ square inches}$).\n\nTherefore, the total surface area of the cube is $6 \\times 144 = 864$ square inches. \n\nSo, the total surface area of a cube with a volume of $1$ cubic foot is $864$ square inches."

'Given that $a$, $b$, and $2009$ form a geometric sequence with an integer ratio, we can express $b$ and $2009$ in terms of $a$ and the common ratio $r$.\n\nThe general form of a geometric sequence is $a, ar, ar^2, ar^3, ...$ where $a$ is the first term and $r$ is the common ratio.\n\nIn this case, we have $a, ar, 2009$ as the terms of the geometric sequence.\n\nSince $b$ is the second term in the sequence, we have $b = ar$.\n\nGiven that $b < 2009$, we have $ar < 2009$.\n\nSince $a < b$, we have $a < ar$, which simplifies to $1 < r$.\n\nSince $r$ is an integer, the smallest possible value for $r$ is $2$.\n\nTherefore, $a < ar < 2009$ becomes $a < 2a < 2009$, which simplifies to $a < 2009$.\n\nSince $a$ is a positive integer, the largest possible value for $a$ is $2008$.\n\nTherefore, the possible values for $a$ are $1, 2, 3, ..., 2008$.\n\nHowever, since $a < b$, the smallest possible value for $a$ is $1$.\n\nTherefore, $a = 1$.\n\nIn conclusion, the value of $a$ is $1$.'

In this case, the perimeter would be $8 + 8 + 15 = 31$ units.\n\nNow, let's simplify the expression \\[\\frac{1}{\\cos^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 40^\\circ}.\\]\n\nRecall the trigonometric identity $\\sin^2 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta = 1$. Rearranging, we get $\\sin^2 \\theta = 1 - \\cos^2 \\theta$ and $\\cos^2 \\theta = 1 - \\sin^2 \\theta$.\n\nSubstitute these identities into the expression:\n\n\\[\\frac{1}{\\cos^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 40^\\circ}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{1}{1 - \\sin^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 40^\\circ}\\]\n\nNow, we can use the Pythagorean trigonometric identity $\\sin^2 \\theta + \\cos^2 \\theta = 1$ to simplify the expression further.\n\n\\[\\frac{1}{1 - \\sin^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 40^\\circ}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{1}{\\cos^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{\\sin^2 40^\\circ}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{1}{\\cos^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{1 - \\cos^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{1 - \\cos^2 40^\\circ}\\]\n\nNow, we can use the reciprocal Pythagorean trigonometric identity $\\csc^2 \\theta = 1 + \\cot^2 \\theta$ to simplify the expression even further.\n\n\\[\\frac{1}{\\cos^2 10^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{1 - \\cos^2 20^\\circ} + \\frac{1}{1 - \\cos^2 40^\\circ}\\]\n\\[= \\csc^2 10^\\circ + \\csc^2 20^\\circ + \\csc^2 40^\\circ\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of the expression is $\\boxed{\\csc^2 10^\\circ + \\csc^2 20^\\circ + \\csc^2 40^\\circ}$."

'To find the smallest positive real number $C$ such that $\\left\\| \\begin{pmatrix} 2 & 3 \\\\ 0 & -2 \\end{pmatrix} \\bold{v} \\right\\| \\le C \\|\\bold{v}\\|$ for all two-dimensional vectors $\\bold{v}$, we need to consider the matrix $\\begin{pmatrix} 2 & 3 \\\\ 0 & -2 \\end{pmatrix}$ as a linear transformation.\n\nThe matrix $\\begin{pmatrix} 2 & 3 \\\\ 0 & -2 \\end{pmatrix}$ represents a counterclockwise rotation followed by a scaling. To find the rotation angle, we can calculate the eigenvalues of the matrix. The characteristic equation is given by:\n\n$\\text{det}\\left(\\begin{pmatrix} 2-\\lambda & 3 \\\\ 0 & -2-\\lambda \\end{pmatrix}\\right) = (2-\\lambda)(-2-\\lambda) = \\lambda^2 - 4 = 0$\n\nSolving this equation gives us $\\lambda = \\pm 2$. Since the eigenvalues are real and distinct, the matrix represents a rotation.\n\nThe rotation angle can be found using the formula $\\theta = \\cos^{-1}\\left(\\frac{\\text{Tr}(A)}{2}\\right)$, where $\\text{Tr}(A)$ is the trace of the matrix. In this case, $\\text{Tr}\\left(\\begin{pmatrix} 2 & 3 \\\\ 0 & -2 \\end{pmatrix}\\right) = 2 - 2 = 0$. Therefore, the rotation angle is $\\theta = \\cos^{-1}(0) = \\frac{\\pi}{2}$.\n\nSince the rotation angle is $\\frac{\\pi}{2}$, the minimum number of degrees the regular pentagon must be rotated until it coincides with its original position is $90$ degrees.\n\nTherefore, the smallest positive real number $C$ such that $\\left\\| \\begin{pmatrix} 2 & 3 \\\\ 0 & -2 \\end{pmatrix} \\bold{v} \\right\\| \\le C \\|\\bold{v}\\|$ for all two-dimensional vectors $\\bold{v}$ is $C = 1$.'

"Let's first find the cost of making a 1 inch cube in terms of the cost of the paint and the cost of the concrete.\n\nLet the cost of the paint be $p$ and the cost of the concrete be $c$.\n\nFor a 1 inch cube, the surface area is $6$ square inches and the volume is $1$ cubic inch. Therefore, the cost of making a 1 inch cube can be expressed as $6p + c = 1.30$.\n\nFor a 2 inch cube, the surface area is $24$ square inches and the volume is $8$ cubic inches. Therefore, the cost of making a 2 inch cube can be expressed as $24p + 8c = 6.80$.\n\nNow, we need to find the values of $p$ and $c. We can solve these two equations simultaneously to find the values of $p$ and $c.\n\nMultiplying the first equation by $8$ and subtracting it from the second equation multiplied by $2$, we get:\n\n$2(24p + 8c) - 8(6p + c) = 2(6.80) - 8(1.30)$\n$48p + 16c - 48p - 8c = 13.60 - 10.40$\n$8c = 3.20$\n$c = 0.40$\n\nSubstitute $c = 0.40$ back into the first equation:\n\n$6p + 0.40 = 1.30$\n$6p = 0.90$\n$p = 0.15$\n\nNow that we have found the values of $p$ and $c, we can find the cost of making a 3 inch cube.\n\nFor a 3 inch cube, the surface area is $54$ square inches and the volume is $27$ cubic inches. Therefore, the cost of making a 3 inch cube can be expressed as $54p + 27c$.\n\nSubstitute $p = 0.15$ and $c = 0.40$ into the equation:\n\n$54(0.15) + 27(0.40) = 8.10 + 10.80 = 18.90$\n\nTherefore, a 3 inch cube would cost $\\$18.90$ to make.\n\nNow, let's find the smallest positive integer $a$ such that $a$, $b$, and $2009$ form a geometric sequence with an integer ratio, where $a<b<2009$.\n\nLet the common ratio be $r$. We need to find the smallest positive integer $a$ such that $a$, $ar$, and $2009$ form a geometric sequence with an integer ratio.\n\nFactorize $2009 = 7^2 \\times 41$.\n\nThe possible values for $a$ are $1, 7, 41$.\n\nTherefore, the smallest positive integer $a$ is $\\boxed{1}$."

'To find the surface area of one of the pieces formed by the plane parallel to edges $AB$ and $CD$ and lying halfway between them, we first need to determine the shape of the resulting piece.\n\nSince the plane is parallel to edges $AB$ and $CD$ and lies halfway between them, it will cut the regular tetrahedron $ABCD$ into two congruent pieces. These pieces will be triangular prisms with a triangular base formed by the intersection of the plane with the faces of the tetrahedron.\n\nThe triangular base will be an isosceles triangle with side lengths of 2, 2, and $\\sqrt{2^2 - 1^2} = \\sqrt{3}$. The height of the prism will be the distance between the plane and the base of the tetrahedron, which can be found using similar triangles. \n\nLet $E$ be the midpoint of $AB$ and $F$ be the midpoint of $CD$. The distance from $E$ to the plane is half the height of the tetrahedron, which is $\\frac{2\\sqrt{6}}{3}$. Similarly, the distance from $F$ to the plane is also $\\frac{2\\sqrt{6}}{3}$. Therefore, the height of the prism is $\\frac{4\\sqrt{6}}{3}$.\n\nThe surface area of one of the pieces is the sum of the areas of the two triangular bases and the three rectangular faces. The area of each triangular base is $\\frac{1}{2} \\times 2 \\times \\sqrt{3} = \\sqrt{3}$. The area of each rectangular face is $2 \\times \\frac{4\\sqrt{6}}{3} = \\frac{8\\sqrt{6}}{3}$. Therefore, the total surface area of one of the pieces is $2\\sqrt{3} + 3 \\times \\frac{8\\sqrt{6}}{3} = 2\\sqrt{3} + 8\\sqrt{6}$.\n\nTherefore, the surface area of one of the pieces formed by the plane parallel to edges $AB$ and $CD$ and lying halfway between them is $2\\sqrt{3} + 8\\sqrt{6}$.'

'To find the value of $k$, we first need to determine the equation of the ellipse $kx^2 + y^2 = 1$ in standard form. The standard form of an ellipse is $\\frac{x^2}{a^2} + \\frac{y^2}{b^2} = 1$, where $a$ and $b$ are the semi-major and semi-minor axes of the ellipse, respectively.\n\nComparing the given equation to the standard form, we have $\\frac{x^2}{\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{k}}} + \\frac{y^2}{1} = 1$. This implies that $a = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{k}}$ and $b = 1$.\n\nThe foci of the ellipse are given by $(\\pm c, 0)$, where $c = \\sqrt{a^2 - b^2}$. In this case, $c = \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{k} - 1}$.\n\nSince the circle passes through the foci $F_1$ and $F_2$ and is tangent to the ellipse at two points on the $x$-axis, the center of the circle lies on the $x$-axis and is equidistant from the foci. Let the center of the circle be $(h, 0)$.\n\nThe distance between the center of the circle and each focus is equal to the radius of the circle. Therefore, we have:\n$\\sqrt{(h - c)^2} = \\sqrt{(h + c)^2} = r$\n\nSolving for $h$ in terms of $c$ and $r$, we get:\n$h - c = r$\n$h + c = r$\n\nAdding these two equations, we get:\n$2h = 2r$\n$h = r$\n\nSince the circle is tangent to the ellipse at two points on the $x$-axis, the distance between the center of the circle and the $x$-axis is equal to the semi-minor axis of the ellipse. Therefore, $b = r = 1$.\n\nSubstitute $b = 1$ into the equation $a = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{k}}$ to get $a = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{k}} = 1$. This implies that $k = 1$.\n\nTherefore, the value of $k$ is $\\boxed{1}$.'

'To solve this problem, we first need to determine the total number of ways in which the 6 girls and 2 boys can sit in a row without any restrictions. \n\nThere are a total of 8 people (6 girls and 2 boys) who need to be seated in a row. The total number of ways to arrange them is 8!, which is equal to 40,320.\n\nNow, we need to consider the restriction that the 2 boys must sit next to each other. We can treat the 2 boys as a single entity, which means there are 7 entities (6 girls + 1 pair of boys) to arrange. The number of ways to arrange these 7 entities is 7!.\n\nHowever, within the pair of boys, there are 2 ways in which the boys can be arranged (Boy1-Boy2 or Boy2-Boy1). Therefore, we need to multiply the number of ways to arrange the 7 entities by 2 to account for this additional arrangement within the pair of boys.\n\nSo, the number of ways in which the 6 girls and 2 boys can sit in a row with the boys sitting next to each other is 7! * 2 = 10,080.\n\nFinally, to find the probability that the boys sit next to each other, we divide the number of favorable outcomes (10,080) by the total number of outcomes (40,320):\n\nProbability = Number of favorable outcomes / Total number of outcomes\nProbability = 10,080 / 40,320\nProbability = 1/4\n\nTherefore, the probability that the 2 boys sit next to each other is 1/4.'
'To find the shortest distance from a point to a line, we can use the formula for the distance between a point $(x_0, y_0)$ and a line $Ax + By + C = 0$, which is given by:\n\n$$\\frac{|Ax_0 + By_0 + C|}{\\sqrt{A^2 + B^2}}$$\n\nIn this case, the point is $(6, 0)$ and the line is $y = 2x - 2$. We can rewrite the equation of the line in the form $Ax + By + C = 0$ as $-2x + y + 2 = 0$. Comparing this to the general form, we have $A = -2$, $B = 1$, $C = 2$, $x_0 = 6$, and $y_0 = 0$. Plugging these values into the formula, we get:\n\n$$\\frac{|-2(6) + 1(0) + 2|}{\\sqrt{(-2)^2 + 1^2}} = \\frac{|-12 + 2|}{\\sqrt{4 + 1}} = \\frac{10}{\\sqrt{5}} = 2\\sqrt{5}$$\n\nTherefore, the shortest distance from the point $(6, 0)$ to the line $y = 2x - 2$ is $2\\sqrt{5}$.'

'To find the original price of the shirt before the $60\\%$ discount, we can set up the following equation:\n\nLet the original price be $x$.\n\nAfter a $60\\%$ discount, the sale price is $0.4x$ (since $100\\% - 60\\% = 40\\%$ or $0.4$).\n\nGiven that the sale price is $\\$14.40$, we can set up the equation:\n\n$0.4x = 14.40$\n\nTo solve for $x$, we divide both sides by $0.4$:\n\n$x = \\frac{14.40}{0.4}$\n\n$x = 36$\n\nTherefore, the original price of the shirt before the $60\\%$ discount was $\\$36.'
"Let's denote the initial number of blue marbles as 4x and the initial number of yellow marbles as 3x. After adding 5 blue marbles and removing 3 yellow marbles, the new number of blue marbles is 4x + 5 and the new number of yellow marbles is 3x - 3.\n\nAccording to the given information, the ratio of blue marbles to yellow marbles after the change is 7:3. This gives us the equation:\n\n(4x + 5) / (3x - 3) = 7 / 3\n\nCross multiplying, we get:\n\n3(4x + 5) = 7(3x - 3)\n12x + 15 = 21x - 21\n36 = 9x\nx = 4\n\nTherefore, the initial number of blue marbles in the bag was 4x = 4 * 4 = 16.\n\nTo find the sum of all prime numbers p for which the congruence 8x  1 (mod p) has no solutions x, we need to consider the cases where the congruence has no solutions. This happens when 8 and p are not coprime, i.e., when p divides 8.\n\nThe prime factors of 8 are 2, so the only prime number p for which the congruence has no solutions is p = 2.\n\nTherefore, the sum of all prime numbers p for which the congruence 8x  1 (mod p) has no solutions x is 2."
"To find the coefficients $p$, $q$, and $r$ of the polynomial $x^9 + px^6 + qx^3 + r$ if $x^3 - 3x^2 + 4x - 1$ is a factor of it, we can use polynomial division.\n\nFirst, let's perform polynomial division of $x^9 + px^6 + qx^3 + r$ by $x^3 - 3x^2 + 4x - 1$:\n\n```\n                    x^6 - 2x^5 -  x^4 +  x^3 +  3x^2 +  4x +  1\n          _______________________________________________________\nx^3 - 3x^2 + 4x - 1 | x^9 + px^6 + qx^3 + r\n                    - (x^9 - 3x^8 + 4x^7 - x^6)\n                    _____________________________\n                           -3x^8 + 4x^7 + px^6\n                           + 3x^8 -  9x^7 + 12x^6\n                           ________________________\n                                  -5x^7 + (p+12)x^6\n                                  + 5x^7 - 15x^6 + 20x^5\n                                  _______________________\n                                         (p-3)x^6 + 20x^5 + qx^3\n                                         - (p-3)x^6 +  9x^5 - 12x^4\n                                         _________________________\n                                                11x^5 + 12x^4 + qx^3\n                                                - 11x^5 + 33x^4 - 44x^3\n                                                _______________________\n                                                      -21x^4 + (q+44)x^3\n                                                      + 21x^4 - 63x^3 + 84x^2\n                                                      _______________________\n                                                             (q-19)x^3 + 84x^2 + r\n                                                             - (q-19)x^3 + 57x^2 - 76x\n                                                             _______________________\n                                                                    27x^2 + 76x + r\n```\n\nSince $x^3 - 3x^2 + 4x - 1$ is a factor of $x^9 + px^6 + qx^3 + r$, the remainder should be zero. Therefore, we have:\n\n$q - 19 = 0 \\implies q = 19$\n\n$27x^2 + 76x + r = 0$\n\nSince this equation must hold for all values of $x$, the coefficients of $x^2$ and $x$ must be zero. Therefore, we have:\n\n$27 = 0 \\implies$ not possible\n\n$76 = 0 \\implies$ not possible\n\nTherefore, there is no solution for $p$, $q$, and $r$ that satisfies the condition that $x^3 - 3x^2 + 4x - 1$ is a factor of $x^9 + px^6 + qx^3 + r$."
'To find the vector $\\mathbf{v}$ with the smallest magnitude in the given equation, we need to find the projection of $\\begin{pmatrix} 90 \\\\ 30 \\\\ 30 \\end{pmatrix}$ onto the plane orthogonal to $\\begin{pmatrix} 1 \\\\ 2 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix}$.\n\nLet $\\mathbf{a} = \\begin{pmatrix} 1 \\\\ 2 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix}$ and $\\mathbf{b} = \\begin{pmatrix} 90 \\\\ 30 \\\\ 30 \\end{pmatrix}$. The vector $\\mathbf{v}$ we are looking for is orthogonal to both $\\mathbf{a}$ and $\\mathbf{b}$.\n\nThe projection of $\\mathbf{b}$ onto the plane orthogonal to $\\mathbf{a}$ is given by $\\text{proj}_{\\mathbf{a}} \\mathbf{b} = \\frac{\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b}}{|\\mathbf{a}|^2} \\mathbf{a}$.\n\nCalculating the dot product $\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b}$:\n$\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b} = 1 \\cdot 90 + 2 \\cdot 30 + (-5) \\cdot 30 = 90 + 60 - 150 = 0$.\n\nCalculating the magnitude of $\\mathbf{a}$:\n$|\\mathbf{a}| = \\sqrt{1^2 + 2^2 + (-5)^2} = \\sqrt{1 + 4 + 25} = \\sqrt{30}$.\n\nTherefore, the projection of $\\mathbf{b}$ onto the plane orthogonal to $\\mathbf{a}$ is:\n$\\text{proj}_{\\mathbf{a}} \\mathbf{b} = \\frac{0}{30} \\begin{pmatrix} 1 \\\\ 2 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix} = \\begin{pmatrix} 0 \\\\ 0 \\\\ 0 \\end{pmatrix}$.\n\nSince the projection is the zero vector, any vector $\\mathbf{v}$ orthogonal to both $\\mathbf{a}$ and $\\mathbf{b}$ will satisfy the given equation. This means there are infinitely many vectors $\\mathbf{v}$ that satisfy the equation, and we cannot determine a unique solution for $\\mathbf{v}$ with the smallest magnitude.\n\nMoving on to the second question, let the three consecutive positive integers be $n-1$, $n$, and $n+1$. Their sum is $3n$, which is a three-digit palindrome less than 220. The largest possible value for $n$ is when $3n = 191$, as this is the largest three-digit palindrome less than 220. Solving for $n$, we get $n = 63$.\n\nTherefore, the three consecutive positive integers are 62, 63, and 64, and the greatest possible value for the largest of these integers is 64.'
"To determine the probability that a triangle can be formed with sides of length 1, $x$, and $y$ when $x$ and $y$ are randomly selected from the interval $(0,3)$, we need to consider the triangle inequality theorem.\n\nAccording to the triangle inequality theorem, the sum of the lengths of any two sides of a triangle must be greater than the length of the third side. In this case, the sides are 1, $x$, and $y$.\n\nFor a triangle to be formed, the following conditions must be met:\n1. $1 + x > y$\n2. $1 + y > x$\n3. $x + y > 1$\n\nLet's analyze each condition separately:\n\n1. $1 + x > y$\nThis condition can be rewritten as $x < 3 - y$.\n\n2. $1 + y > x$\nThis condition can be rewritten as $y < 3 - x$.\n\n3. $x + y > 1$\nThis condition can be rewritten as $x > 1 - y$ and $y > 1 - x$.\n\nTo visualize the valid region for $x$ and $y$ that satisfy all three conditions, we can plot the inequalities on a graph. The valid region will be the intersection of the regions defined by the inequalities.\n\nThe valid region will be a triangle with vertices at (1,1), (1,2), and (2,1) in the xy-plane.\n\nThe area of this triangle can be calculated using geometry. The base and height of the triangle are both 1 unit, so the area is 0.5 * base * height = 0.5 * 1 * 1 = 0.5 square units.\n\nSince the total area of the region where $x$ and $y$ can be selected from is 9 square units (3 * 3), the probability of randomly selecting $x$ and $y$ such that a triangle can be formed is the area of the valid region (0.5 square units) divided by the total area, which is 0.5/9 = 1/18.\n\nTherefore, the probability that a triangle can be formed with sides of length 1, $x$, and $y$ when $x$ and $y$ are randomly selected from the interval $(0,3)$ is 1/18."
"To find the greater of the two consecutive positive even integers whose product is 288, we can set up an equation. Let's denote the smaller integer as x and the greater integer as x + 2 (since they are consecutive even integers).\n\nAccording to the given information, we have:\nx(x + 2) = 288\n\nExpanding the left side of the equation:\nx^2 + 2x = 288\n\nRearranging the equation into a quadratic form:\nx^2 + 2x - 288 = 0\n\nNow, we can solve this quadratic equation to find the values of x. Factoring the quadratic equation:\n(x + 18)(x - 16) = 0\n\nSetting each factor to zero:\nx + 18 = 0   or   x - 16 = 0\nx = -18        or   x = 16\n\nSince we are looking for positive even integers, we discard the negative solution. Therefore, the smaller integer is 16 and the greater integer is 16 + 2 = 18.\n\nTherefore, the greater of the two integers is 18.\n\nNow, let's find the complex number that results from a $90^\\circ$ counter-clockwise rotation around the origin of the complex number $7 + 2i$.\n\nTo rotate a complex number $a + bi$ by $90^\\circ$ counter-clockwise, we can multiply it by $i$.\n\nGiven complex number: $7 + 2i$\n\nRotated complex number: $(7 + 2i)i = 7i + 2i^2$\n\nSince $i^2 = -1$, we can simplify:\n$7i + 2(-1) = 7i - 2 = -2 + 7i$\n\nTherefore, the complex number that results from a $90^\\circ$ counter-clockwise rotation around the origin of the complex number $7 + 2i$ is $-2 + 7i$."
'Given the equation $3x + 2y = 12$, we are asked to find the value of $b$ when $a = 4$. \n\nTo find the value of $b$, we first need to solve for $y$ in terms of $x$ in the given equation. \n\n$3x + 2y = 12$\n\n$2y = 12 - 3x$\n\n$y = \\frac{12 - 3x}{2}$\n\nNow, we substitute $a = 4$ into the equation:\n\n$y = \\frac{12 - 3(4)}{2}$\n\n$y = \\frac{12 - 12}{2}$\n\n$y = \\frac{0}{2}$\n\n$y = 0$\n\nTherefore, when $a = 4$, the value of $b$ is $0$.'
'To find the value of $(\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{3})^3$, we can expand it using the binomial theorem. \n\n$(\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{3})^3 = (\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{3})(\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{3})(\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{3})$\n\nExpanding this expression, we get:\n\n$= (\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{3})(2\\sqrt{3}+3\\sqrt{2}+2\\sqrt{2}+3\\sqrt{3})$\n\n$= 2\\sqrt{6} + 3\\sqrt{4} + 2\\sqrt{3} + 3\\sqrt{6} + 3\\sqrt{2} + 2\\sqrt{3}$\n\n$= 2\\sqrt{6} + 6 + 2\\sqrt{3} + 3\\sqrt{6} + 3\\sqrt{2}$\n\nNow, we can write this in the form $a\\sqrt{2} + b\\sqrt{3} + c\\sqrt{6}$:\n\n$a = 0$ (since there is no $\\sqrt{2}$ term)\n$b = 2 + 3 = 5$\n$c = 2 + 3 = 5$\n\nTherefore, $a+b+c = 0 + 5 + 5 = 10$.\n\nSo, the value of $a+b+c$ is 10.'
"From the given equation $z + \\frac{1}{z} = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}$, we can rewrite it as $z^2 + 1 = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}z$. Multiplying both sides by $z$, we get $z^3 + z = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}z^2$.\n\nNow, let's consider the function $f(x) = x^3 + x$. We want to find real numbers $a \\neq 0$ and $b$ such that $f(x) - f(a) = (x - a)^2 (x - b)$.\n\nExpanding $f(x) - f(a)$, we have:\n$f(x) - f(a) = (x^3 + x) - (a^3 + a) = x^3 + x - a^3 - a = x^3 - a^3 + x - a = (x - a)(x^2 + ax + a^2 + 1)$.\n\nComparing this with $(x - a)^2 (x - b)$, we see that $b = a^2 + 1$.\n\nTherefore, in our case, $a = z$ and $b = z^2 + 1$. We are asked to find $z^{85} + \\frac{1}{z^{85}}$.\n\nNow, let's consider the expression $(z^{85} + \\frac{1}{z^{85}})(z^2 + 1)$. Therefore, $z^{87} = z^{85} \\cdot z^2 = z^{85}(\\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}z^2 - z)$.\n\nSubstitute this back into our expression, we get:\n$z^{87} + z^{85} + \\frac{1}{z^{85}} + \\frac{1}{z^{87}} = z^{85}(\\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}z^2 - z) + z^{85} + \\frac{1}{z^{85}} + \\frac{1}{z^{85}(\\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}z^2 - z)}$.\n\nSimplify this expression to get the final answer."

'To convert the point $(0,3)$ in rectangular coordinates to polar coordinates, we can use the formulas:\n\n$r = \\sqrt{x^2 + y^2}$\n\n$\\theta = \\arctan\\left(\\frac{y}{x}\\right)$\n\nGiven that the point is $(0,3)$, we have $x = 0$ and $y = 3$. \n\nTherefore, $r = \\sqrt{0^2 + 3^2} = \\sqrt{9} = 3$.\n\nSince $x = 0$ and $y = 3$, the point is in the second quadrant. Therefore, we need to adjust the angle by adding $\\pi$ to the angle calculated by $\\arctan\\left(\\frac{3}{0}\\right) = \\frac{\\pi}{2}$.\n\nSo, $\\theta = \\frac{\\pi}{2} + \\pi = \\frac{3\\pi}{2}$.\n\nTherefore, the point $(0,3)$ in rectangular coordinates is equivalent to $(3, \\frac{3\\pi}{2})$ in polar coordinates.'
"Given the parameterization of the curve as $(x,y) = (t^3 + 7, -3t^2 - 6t - 5)$, we are asked to find the point the curve passes through at $t = 2$.\n\nWhen $t = 2$, we can substitute $t = 2$ into the parameterization to find the corresponding point on the curve:\n\\[x = 2^3 + 7 = 15\\]\n\\[y = -3(2)^2 - 6(2) - 5 = -3(4) - 6(2) - 5 = -12 - 12 - 5 = -29\\]\n\nTherefore, when $t = 2$, the curve passes through the point $(15, -29)$.\n\nNow, let's simplify the expression \\[\\frac{\\sec x}{\\sin x} - \\frac{\\sin x}{\\cos x}.\\]\n\nFirst, recall that $\\sec x = \\frac{1}{\\cos x}$ and $\\cot x = \\frac{\\cos x}{\\sin x}$.\n\nSubstitute these into the expression:\n\\[\\frac{\\frac{1}{\\cos x}}{\\sin x} - \\frac{\\sin x}{\\cos x} = \\frac{1}{\\cos x \\cdot \\sin x} - \\frac{\\sin^2 x}{\\cos x}\\]\n\nNow, recall that $\\sin^2 x + \\cos^2 x = 1$, so $\\sin^2 x = 1 - \\cos^2 x$.\n\nSubstitute this into the expression:\n\\[\\frac{1}{\\cos x \\cdot \\sin x} - \\frac{1 - \\cos^2 x}{\\cos x} = \\frac{1}{\\cos x \\cdot \\sin x} - \\frac{1}{\\cos x} + \\frac{\\cos x}{\\cos x}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{1}{\\cos x \\cdot \\sin x} - \\frac{1}{\\cos x} + 1\\]\n\nTherefore, the simplified expression is \\[\\frac{1}{\\cos x \\cdot \\sin x} - \\frac{1}{\\cos x} + 1\\]."
'Given that angle A is 14 degrees and AB is a diameter of the circle in which the triangle is inscribed, we can conclude that angle B is a right angle (90 degrees). This is because an angle inscribed in a semicircle is always a right angle.\n\nTherefore, the measure of angle B in triangle ABC is 90 degrees.'
'Given the expression $\\frac{(a + b + c)[(a + b)^2 + (a + b + 4c)^2]}{abc}$, we can simplify it by expanding the terms inside the brackets:\n\n\\[(a + b)^2 = a^2 + 2ab + b^2\\]\n\\[(a + b + 4c)^2 = a^2 + 2ab + 16c^2 + 2a(4c) + 2b(4c) + 16c^2 = a^2 + 2ab + 16c^2 + 8a + 8b + 16c\\]\n\nNow, substitute these back into the expression:\n\n\\[\\frac{(a + b + c)[(a + b)^2 + (a + b + 4c)^2]}{abc} = \\frac{(a + b + c)(a^2 + 2ab + b^2 + a^2 + 2ab + 16c^2 + 8a + 8b + 16c)}{abc}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{(a + b + c)(2a^2 + 4ab + b^2 + 16c^2 + 8a + 8b + 16c)}{abc}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{2a^3 + 4a^2b + ab^2 + 16ac^2 + 8a^2 + 16ab + 8b^2 + 16bc + 2a^2c + 4abc + b^2c + 16c^3}{abc}\\]\n\\[= \\frac{2a^2 + 4ab + b^2 + 16c^2 + 8a + 16c + 8b + 16c + 2a^2/c + 4ab/c + b^2/c + 16c^2/a}{abc}\\]\n\nNow, we need to find the minimum value of this expression. To do this, we can use the AM-GM Inequality:\n\nFor positive real numbers $x_1, x_2, ..., x_n$, the AM-GM Inequality states that:\n\\[\\frac{x_1 + x_2 + ... + x_n}{n} \\geq \\sqrt[n]{x_1x_2...x_n}\\]\n\nApplying this inequality to our expression, we get:\n\\[\\frac{2a^2 + 4ab + b^2 + 16c^2 + 8a + 16c + 8b + 16c + 2a^2/c + 4ab/c + b^2/c + 16c^2/a}{12} \\geq \\sqrt[12]{2a^2 \\cdot 4ab \\cdot b^2 \\cdot 16c^2 \\cdot 8a \\cdot 16c \\cdot 8b \\cdot 16c \\cdot 2a^2/c \\cdot 4ab/c \\cdot b^2/c \\cdot 16c^2/a}\\]\n\nSolving this inequality will give us the minimum value of the expression.'
'To find $f\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{3}\\right) + f(\\sqrt{45}) + f(8^{2/3})$, we need to evaluate $f(n)$ for each of the given values.\n\n1. For $n = \\frac{\\pi}{3}$:\nSince $\\frac{\\pi}{3} < 4$, we use the second case of the function definition:\n$f\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{3}\\right) = \\lceil \\frac{\\pi}{3} \\rceil = 2$.\n\n2. For $n = \\sqrt{45}$:\nSince $\\sqrt{45} \\geq 4$, we use the first case of the function definition:\n$f(\\sqrt{45}) = \\lfloor \\sqrt{45} \\rfloor = \\lfloor 6.7082039325 \\rfloor = 6$.\n\n3. For $n = 8^{2/3}$:\nSince $8^{2/3} = 4$, we use the first case of the function definition:\n$f(8^{2/3}) = \\lfloor 4 \\rfloor = 4$.\n\nTherefore, $f\\left(\\frac{\\pi}{3}\\right) + f(\\sqrt{45}) + f(8^{2/3}) = 2 + 6 + 4 = 12$.\n\nThe sum of the two possible values of $c$ that satisfy the conditions given in the problem is $12$.'

'To find the projection of vector $\\mathbf{a}$ onto vector $\\mathbf{b}$, we first need to calculate the magnitude of vector $\\mathbf{b}$, denoted as $||\\mathbf{b}||$. The magnitude of a vector $\\mathbf{v} = \\begin{pmatrix} v_1 \\\\ v_2 \\\\ v_3 \\end{pmatrix}$ is given by $||\\mathbf{v}|| = \\sqrt{v_1^2 + v_2^2 + v_3^2}$.\n\nFor $\\mathbf{b} = \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 6 \\\\ 3 \\end{pmatrix}$, we have:\n$||\\mathbf{b}|| = \\sqrt{2^2 + 6^2 + 3^2} = \\sqrt{4 + 36 + 9} = \\sqrt{49} = 7$.\n\nNext, we calculate the projection of $\\mathbf{a}$ onto $\\mathbf{b}$ using the formula:\n$\\text{proj}_{\\mathbf{b}}(\\mathbf{a}) = \\left(\\frac{\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b}}{||\\mathbf{b}||^2}\\right)\\mathbf{b}$.\n\nGiven that the dot product of $\\mathbf{a}$ and $\\mathbf{b}$ is 8, we have $\\mathbf{a} \\cdot \\mathbf{b} = 8$.\n\nPlugging in the values, we get:\n$\\text{proj}_{\\mathbf{b}}(\\mathbf{a}) = \\left(\\frac{8}{7^2}\\right)\\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 6 \\\\ 3 \\end{pmatrix} = \\frac{8}{49}\\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 6 \\\\ 3 \\end{pmatrix} = \\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{16}{49} \\\\ \\frac{48}{49} \\\\ \\frac{24}{49} \\end{pmatrix}$.\n\nTherefore, the projection of vector $\\mathbf{a}$ onto vector $\\mathbf{b} = \\begin{pmatrix} 2 \\\\ 6 \\\\ 3 \\end{pmatrix}$ given that their dot product is 8 is $\\begin{pmatrix} \\frac{16}{49} \\\\ \\frac{48}{49} \\\\ \\frac{24}{49} \\end{pmatrix}$.'
'To find the smallest positive integer multiple of 30 that can be formed using only the digits 0 and 2, we need to consider the factors of 30, which are 2, 3, 5, and 6.\n\nSince we can only use the digits 0 and 2, we need to find a combination of these digits that can form a multiple of 30. \n\nThe smallest multiple of 30 that can be formed using only the digits 0 and 2 is 20. This is because 20 is a multiple of 2 and 5, which are factors of 30. \n\nTherefore, the smallest positive integer multiple of 30 that can be formed using only the digits 0 and 2 is 20.'
'Given that $\\overline{AB}\\|\\overline{DE}$, we can see that $\\triangle ABC$ and $\\triangle CDE$ are similar triangles. \n\nSince $BD=4BC$, we can set $BC=x$ and $BD=4x$. Therefore, $CD=5x$.\n\nSince the area of $\\triangle ABC$ is 6 square centimeters, we have:\n\n$\\frac{1}{2} \\cdot BC \\cdot AC = 6$\n\n$\\frac{1}{2} \\cdot x \\cdot (5x) = 6$\n\n$\\frac{5}{2}x^2 = 6$\n\n$x^2 = \\frac{12}{5}$\n\n$x = \\sqrt{\\frac{12}{5}} = \\frac{2\\sqrt{15}}{5}$\n\nTherefore, the area of $\\triangle CDE$ can be calculated as:\n\n$\\frac{1}{2} \\cdot CD \\cdot CE = \\frac{1}{2} \\cdot 5x \\cdot 5x = \\frac{25}{2}x^2 = \\frac{25}{2} \\cdot \\frac{12}{5} = 30$\n\nSo, the area of $\\triangle CDE$ is 30 square centimeters.\n\nTo find the greatest possible value of the greatest common divisor of $n + 7$ and $2n + 1$, we can use the Euclidean algorithm.\n\n$2n + 1 = 2(n+7) - 13$\n\n$n+7 = (n+7) - 0$\n\nTherefore, the greatest common divisor of $n + 7$ and $2n + 1$ is 13.\n\nTherefore, the answer is $\\boxed{13}$.'
"First, we need to calculate the force exerted by Jack when throwing the baseball and the force Jen needs to exert to throw the softball with the same force.\n\nGiven:\nMass of softball (m1) = 200 g = 0.2 kg\nMass of baseball (m2) = 150 g = 0.15 kg\n\nLet F1 be the force exerted by Jack when throwing the baseball.\nLet F2 be the force Jen needs to exert to throw the softball with the same force.\n\nAccording to the formula F = ma, we have:\nF1 = m1 * a1\nF2 = m2 * a2\n\nSince Jen wants to throw the softball with the same force as Jack throws the baseball, we have:\nF1 = F2\nm1 * a1 = m2 * a2\n0.2 * a1 = 0.15 * a2\na1/a2 = 0.15/0.2\na1/a2 = 3/4\n\nTherefore, the ratio of acceleration of Jen's ball to Jack's is 3/4."
'To find the polar coordinates of the point $(0,3)$ in rectangular coordinates, we first need to convert the point from rectangular coordinates $(x,y)$ to polar coordinates $(r,\\theta)$.\n\nGiven that the point is $(0,3)$, we can see that the distance $r$ from the origin to the point is simply the value of $y$, which is 3. The angle $\\theta$ that the line connecting the origin and the point makes with the positive x-axis is $\\frac{\\pi}{2}$ (or 90 degrees).\n\nTherefore, the polar coordinates of the point $(0,3)$ in rectangular coordinates are $(3, \\frac{\\pi}{2})$.'

'To find the value of $9 \\& 2$ using the bitwise AND operation, we first need to convert 9 and 2 into binary form.\n\n9 in binary is 1001 and 2 in binary is 0010.\n\nPerforming the bitwise AND operation on 1001 and 0010:\n\n```\n  1001\n& 0010\n-------\n  0000\n```\n\nTherefore, the value of $9 \\& 2$ under the given operation $\\&$ is 0.'
"To find the dot product of two vectors, we multiply the corresponding components of the vectors and then sum up the results. \n\nGiven vectors:\n$\\begin{pmatrix} -2 \\\\ 0 \\\\ 7 \\end{pmatrix}$ and $\\begin{pmatrix} 3 \\\\ 4 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix}$\n\nThe dot product is calculated as follows:\n$(-2)(3) + (0)(4) + (7)(-5) = -6 + 0 - 35 = -41$\n\nTherefore, the dot product of the two vectors is -41.\n\nNow, let's move on to the second part of the question.\n\nWe are given the expression $\\frac{(a + b + c)[(a + b)^2 + (a + b + 4c)^2]}{abc}$ and we need to find the minimum value for positive real numbers $a, b,$ and $c$.\n\nExpanding the expression, we get:\n$\\frac{(a + b + c)(a^2 + 2ab + b^2 + a^2 + 2ab + b^2 + 8ac + 8bc + 16c^2)}{abc}$\n$\\frac{(2a^2 + 4ab + 2b^2 + 8ac + 8bc + 16c^2)}{abc}$\n$\\frac{2(a^2 + 2ab + b^2) + 8(ac + bc + 2c^2)}{abc}$\n$\\frac{2(a + b)^2 + 8c(a + b + 2c)}{abc}$\n\nTo find the minimum value of this expression, we can use the AM-GM inequality. \nBy AM-GM inequality, we have:\n$\\frac{2(a + b)^2 + 8c(a + b + 2c)}{abc} \\geq 3\\sqrt[3]{2(a + b)^2 \\cdot 8c(a + b + 2c)}$\n\nSimplifying the right side of the inequality:\n$3\\sqrt[3]{16c(a + b)^3(a + b + 2c)}$\n$3\\sqrt[3]{16abc(a + b)(a + b + 2c)}$\n\nTherefore, the minimum value of the expression is $3\\sqrt[3]{16abc(a + b)(a + b + 2c)}$."

"To determine the probability that the checker is placed on a shaded square of the checkerboard, we need to consider all possible outcomes when spinning the wheel twice.\n\n1. The first spin of the wheel can result in any number from 1 to 10 with equal probability.\n2. The second spin of the wheel can also result in any number from 1 to 10 with equal probability.\n\nWhen the first number is divided by 4, the remainders can be 1, 2, or 3. When the second number is divided by 5, the remainders can be 1, 2, 3, or 4. This creates a total of 3 * 4 = 12 possible outcomes.\n\nNow, let's determine which of these outcomes result in the checker being placed on a shaded square:\n\nShaded squares on the checkerboard:\n- (3,1), (3,-1), (4,1), (4,-1), (5,0), (5,-2)\n\nOut of the 12 possible outcomes, the following outcomes result in the checker being placed on a shaded square:\n- (3,1), (3,-1), (4,1), (4,-1), (5,0), (5,-2)\n\nTherefore, the probability that the checker is placed on a shaded square of the checkerboard is 6/12 = 1/2.\n\nIn conclusion, the probability that the checker is placed on a shaded square of the checkerboard is 1/2."
"Given that in right triangle $ABC$ with $\\angle B = 90^\\circ$, we have $\\sin A = 2\\cos A$. We need to find $\\tan A$.\n\nFrom the given information, we know that $\\sin A = \\frac{BC}{AC}$ and $\\cos A = \\frac{AB}{AC}$.\n\nSince $\\sin A = 2\\cos A$, we have $\\frac{BC}{AC} = 2 \\cdot \\frac{AB}{AC}$.\n\nSimplifying, we get $BC = 2AB$.\n\nNow, in a right triangle, we have $BC^2 = AB^2 + AC^2$ (by the Pythagorean theorem).\n\nSubstitute $BC = 2AB$ into the equation above:\n\n$(2AB)^2 = AB^2 + AC^2$\n\n$4AB^2 = AB^2 + AC^2$\n\n$3AB^2 = AC^2$\n\n$AC = AB\\sqrt{3}$\n\nNow, we can find $\\tan A$:\n\n$\\tan A = \\frac{\\sin A}{\\cos A} = \\frac{2\\cos A}{\\cos A} = 2$\n\nTherefore, $\\tan A = 2$.\n\nNow, let's move on to the second question:\n\nIf Suzanne walks four miles every third day, then in February (which has 28 days), she will walk four miles on 9 days (since 28 divided by 3 is approximately 9 with a remainder).\n\nTherefore, the fewest number of miles Suzanne can walk in February is $4 \\text{ miles/day} \\times 9 \\text{ days} = 36 \\text{ miles}$."
"Let $a = \\sqrt{x + \\sqrt{3x + 6}}$ and $b = \\sqrt{x - \\sqrt{3x + 6}}$. \n\nFrom the given equation, we have $a + b = 6$. Squaring both sides, we get $a^2 + 2ab + b^2 = 36$.\n\nNow, let's consider $a^2 + b^2$. We have:\n\\[a^2 + b^2 = (a + b)^2 - 2ab = 6^2 - 2ab = 36 - 2ab\\]\n\nSubstitute this back into the equation $a^2 + 2ab + b^2 = 36$, we get:\n\\[36 - 2ab + 2ab = 36\\]\n\\[36 = 36\\]\n\nThis means that the equation holds true for all values of $x$. "The equation given, $\\left(\\frac x2 - 3\\right)^2 + y^2 = 10$, represents an ellipse.\n\nTo understand why this equation represents an ellipse, let's analyze the general form of the equation of an ellipse:\n\n$\\frac{(x-h)^2}{a^2} + \\frac{(y-k)^2}{b^2} = 1$\n\nComparing this general form with the given equation $\\left(\\frac x2 - 3\\right)^2 + y^2 = 10$, we can see that:\n- $h = 3$ (center of the ellipse in the x-direction)\n- $k = 0$ (center of the ellipse in the y-direction)\n- $a^2 = 10$ (square of the semi-major axis)\n- $b^2 = 10$ (square of the semi-minor axis)\n\nSince $a^2 = b^2$, the ellipse is a circle. The center of the circle is at the point (3, 0) and the radius of the circle is $\\sqrt{10}$. Therefore, the graph of the equation $\\left(\\frac x2 - 3\\right)^2 + y^2 = 10$ represents a circle."
"To find out how many students participate in both MATHCOUNTS and science club, we can use the principle of inclusion-exclusion. \n\nLet's denote:\n- A as the set of students participating in MATHCOUNTS (28 students)\n- B as the set of students participating in the science club (21 students)\n- U as the universal set of all students in the class (50 students)\n- N as the set of students participating in neither activity (6 students)\n\nWe want to find the number of students in the intersection of sets A and B, which represents students participating in both MATHCOUNTS and the science club.\n\nBy the principle of inclusion-exclusion:\n|A  B| = |A| + |B| - |A  B| + |N|\n\nWhere |A  B| represents the total number of students participating in either MATHCOUNTS or the science club.\n\nSubstitute the given values:\n|A  B| = 28 + 21 - |A  B| + 6\n|A  B| = 49 - |A  B| + 6\n|A  B| = 55 - |A  B|\n\nSince the total number of students in the class is 50 (U), we have:\n|A  B| = |U| - |N|\n|A  B| = 50 - 6\n|A  B| = 44\n\nSubstitute back into the equation:\n44 = 55 - |A  B|\n|A  B| = 55 - 44\n|A  B| = 11\n\nTherefore, there are 11 students who participate in both MATHCOUNTS and the science club."
"To find the smallest positive multiple of 450 whose digits are all zeroes and ones, we need to consider the factors of 450 and the pattern of digits in multiples of 450.\n\nFirst, let's find the prime factorization of 450:\n450 = 2 * 3^2 * 5^2\n\nMultiples of 450 will have the same prime factors, but with different powers. Since we are looking for a multiple with digits that are all zeroes and ones, we need to consider the possible combinations of powers of 2, 3, and 5 that will result in a number with only zeroes and ones.\n\nThe number formed by all ones is 111...1, which is equivalent to (10^n - 1)/9, where n is the number of ones. This means that the number formed by all ones is a multiple of 9.\n\nSince 450 = 2 * 3^2 * 5^2, any multiple of 450 will also be a multiple of 9. Therefore, the smallest positive multiple of 450 whose digits are all zeroes and ones must be a multiple of 9.\n\nThe smallest multiple of 450 that is also a multiple of 9 is the least common multiple (LCM) of 450 and 9. To find the LCM, we need to consider the highest power of each prime factor in the prime factorization of 450 and 9:\n\n450 = 2 * 3^2 * 5^2\n9 = 3^2\n\nThe LCM will be the product of the highest powers of each prime factor:\nLCM = 2 * 3^2 * 5^2 = 450\n\nTherefore, the smallest positive multiple of 450 whose digits are all zeroes and ones is 450 itself."
'The dot product of two vectors $\\mathbf{v} = \\begin{pmatrix} v_1 \\\\ v_2 \\\\ v_3 \\end{pmatrix}$ and $\\mathbf{w} = \\begin{pmatrix} w_1 \\\\ w_2 \\\\ w_3 \\end{pmatrix}$ is given by $\\mathbf{v} \\cdot \\mathbf{w} = v_1w_1 + v_2w_2 + v_3w_3$.\n\nIn this case, the vectors are $\\begin{pmatrix} -2 \\\\ 0 \\\\ 7 \\end{pmatrix}$ and $\\begin{pmatrix} 3 \\\\ 4 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix}$.\n\nTherefore, the dot product is:\n\\[\\begin{pmatrix} -2 \\\\ 0 \\\\ 7 \\end{pmatrix} \\cdot \\begin{pmatrix} 3 \\\\ 4 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix} = (-2)(3) + (0)(4) + (7)(-5) = -6 + 0 - 35 = -41.\\]\n\nSo, the dot product of the vectors $\\begin{pmatrix} -2 \\\\ 0 \\\\ 7 \\end{pmatrix}$ and $\\begin{pmatrix} 3 \\\\ 4 \\\\ -5 \\end{pmatrix}$ is $\\boxed{-41}$.'

"To find the largest possible area of the rectangular field enclosed by the athletic track, we need to consider that the track is rectangular in shape and the total length of the track is 400 meters. \n\nLet's denote the length of the rectangular field as L and the width as W. Since the track is rectangular, the total length of the track is equal to the perimeter of the rectangular field, which is given as 400 meters. \n\nTherefore, we have the equation: 2L + 2W = 400\n\nTo find the largest possible area of the rectangular field, we need to maximize the area A, which is given by A = L * W.\n\nWe can rewrite the equation for the perimeter as: L + W = 200\n\nNow, we can express one of the variables in terms of the other to maximize the area. Let's express W in terms of L: W = 200 - L\n\nSubstitute W = 200 - L into the area equation: A = L * (200 - L) = 200L - L^2\n\nTo find the maximum area, we need to find the vertex of the parabolic function A = -L^2 + 200L. The vertex of a parabola in the form A = ax^2 + bx + c is given by x = -b / 2a. In this case, a = -1 and b = 200.\n\nTherefore, the L value that maximizes the area is L = -200 / (2*(-1)) = 100\n\nSubstitute L = 100 back into the equation W = 200 - L: W = 200 - 100 = 100\n\nSo, the largest possible area of the rectangular field enclosed by the athletic track is A = L * W = 100 * 100 = 10000 square meters."

'Given that $\\sin A = 2\\cos A$, we can use the Pythagorean identity $\\sin^2 A + \\cos^2 A = 1$ to find the value of $\\tan A$.\n\nSince $\\sin A = 2\\cos A$, we have:\n\\[\\sin^2 A = (2\\cos A)^2 = 4\\cos^2 A\\]\nSubstitute this into the Pythagorean identity:\n\\[4\\cos^2 A + \\cos^2 A = 1\\]\n\\[5\\cos^2 A = 1\\]\n\\[\\cos^2 A = \\frac{1}{5}\\]\n\\[\\cos A = \\pm \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}}\\]\n\nSince $\\angle B = 90^\\circ$, we have a right triangle $ABC$ with $\\angle A$ as the acute angle. Therefore, $\\cos A$ is positive. Thus, $\\cos A = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}}$.\n\nNow, we can find $\\sin A$ using $\\sin A = 2\\cos A$:\n\\[\\sin A = 2 \\cdot \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}} = \\frac{2}{\\sqrt{5}} = \\frac{2\\sqrt{5}}{5}\\]\n\nFinally, we can find $\\tan A$ using the definition of tangent:\n\\[\\tan A = \\frac{\\sin A}{\\cos A} = \\frac{\\frac{2\\sqrt{5}}{5}}{\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}}} = 2\\]\n\nTherefore, in right triangle $ABC$ with $\\angle B = 90^\\circ$ and $\\sin A = 2\\cos A$, the value of $\\tan A$ is $\\boxed{2}$.'

'Given:\n1. $\\log_6 (x-y) + \\log_6 (x+y) = 2$\n2. $\\log_y 5x = 2$\n\nFrom the first equation, we can use the product rule of logarithms to combine the two logarithms:\n$\\log_6 ((x-y)(x+y)) = 2$\n$\\log_6 (x^2 - y^2) = 2$\n$x^2 - y^2 = 6^2$\n$x^2 - y^2 = 36$\n$(x-y)(x+y) = 36$\n\nFrom the second equation, we can rewrite it using the change of base formula:\n$\\frac{\\log 5x}{\\log y} = 2$\n$\\frac{\\log 5 + \\log x}{\\log y} = 2$\n$\\frac{\\log 5}{\\log y} + \\frac{\\log x}{\\log y} = 2$\n$\\log_y 5 + \\log_y x = 2$\n$\\log_y (5x) = 2$\n$5x = y^2$\n\nSubstitute $5x = y^2$ into $(x-y)(x+y) = 36$:\n$(y^2 - y)(y^2 + y) = 36$\n$y(y-1)(y+1)(y+1) = 36$\n$y(y-1)^2(y+1) = 36$\n\nSince $\\log_y 5x = 2$, we have $5x = y^2$. Substitute $5x = y^2$ into $y(y-1)^2(y+1) = 36$:\n$5(y-1)^2(y+1) = 36$\n$5(y^2 - 2y + 1)(y+1) = 36$\n$5y^3 + 5y^2 - 10y^2 - 10y + 5y + 5 = 36$\n$5y^3 - 5y - 31 = 0$\n\nBy trial and error, we find that $y = 2$ satisfies the equation. Therefore, $5x = 2^2$ and $x = \\frac{4}{5}$.\n\nNow, we need to find $f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right)$ where $f(x) = 5x$. The inverse function of $f(x) = 5x$ is $f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{x}{5}$. Therefore, $f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) = \\frac{\\frac{1}{5}}{5} = \\frac{1}{25}$. \n\nSo, the value of $f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right)$ is $\\frac{1}{25}$.'
"Given that $F(z)=\\frac{z+i}{z-i}$ for all complex numbers $z\\not= i,$ and $z_n=F(z_{n-1})$ for all positive integers $n,$ we can find $z_{2002}$ by repeatedly applying the function $F(z)$ starting from $z_0=\\frac{1}{137}+i.$\n\nFirst, let's find $z_1$:\n$z_1=F(z_0)=F\\left(\\frac{1}{137}+i\\right)=\\frac{\\frac{1}{137}+i+i}{\\frac{1}{137}+i-i}=\\frac{\\frac{1}{137}+2i}{\\frac{1}{137}}=1+274i.$\n\nNext, let's find $z_2$:\n$z_2=F(z_1)=F(1+274i)=\\frac{1+274i+i}{1+274i-i}=\\frac{1+275i}{1+273i}=\\frac{(1+275i)(1-273i)}{(1+273i)(1-273i)}=\\frac{1+275i-273i-75025}{1+273^2}=\\frac{-75024+2i}{75026}=-\\frac{37512}{37513}+\\frac{1}{37513}i.$\n\nContinuing this process, we find that $z_{2002}=-\\frac{37512}{37513}+\\frac{1}{37513}i.$\n\nNow, to find the area of a triangle with sides measuring 5, 5, and 6 units, we can use Heron's formula. Let $a=5, b=5,$ and $c=6.$\n\nThe semi-perimeter $s$ is given by $s=\\frac{a+b+c}{2}=\\frac{5+5+6}{2}=8.$\n\nUsing Heron's formula, the area $A$ of the triangle is given by:\n$A=\\sqrt{s(s-a)(s-b)(s-c)}=\\sqrt{8(8-5)(8-5)(8-6)}=\\sqrt{8(3)(3)(2)}=\\sqrt{144}=12.$\n\nTherefore, the area of the triangle with sides measuring 5, 5, and 6 units is 12 square units."
